</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Rights" title="Template:Rights"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Rights" title="Template talk:Rights"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Rights&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Magna_Carta_(British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4800" data-file-width="7200" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg/250px-Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg/375px-Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg/500px-Magna_Carta_%28British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Magna_Carta_(British_Library_Cotton_MS_Augustus_II.106).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Magna_Carta" title="Magna Carta">Magna Carta</a></i> or "Great Charter" was one of the world's first documents containing commitments by a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign" title="Sovereign">sovereign</a> to his people to respect certain legal rights.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Human rights</b> are <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">moral</a> principles or <a href="/wiki/Social_norm" title="Social norm">norms</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordEncy_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordEncy-1">[1]</a></sup> for certain standards of <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">human</a> behaviour and are regularly protected in <a href="/wiki/Municipal_law" title="Municipal law">municipal</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENickel2010_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENickel2010-2">[2]</a></sup> They are commonly understood as inalienable,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsUnitedNations_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsUnitedNations-3">[3]</a></sup> fundamental <a href="/wiki/Rights" title="Rights">rights</a> "to which a person is inherently entitled simply because she or he is a human being"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESepulvedavan_BanningGudmundsdottirChamoun20043_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESepulvedavan_BanningGudmundsdottirChamoun20043-4">[4]</a></sup> and which are "inherent in all human beings",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsBritannica_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsBritannica-5">[5]</a></sup> regardless of their age, ethnic origin, location, language, religion, ethnicity, or any other status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsUnitedNations_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsUnitedNations-3">[3]</a></sup> They are applicable everywhere and at every time in the sense of being <a href="/wiki/Universality_(philosophy)" title="Universality (philosophy)">universal</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordEncy_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordEncy-1">[1]</a></sup> and they are <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarian</a> in the sense of being the same for everyone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsUnitedNations_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-twsUnitedNations-3">[3]</a></sup> They are regarded as requiring empathy and the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsGaryJBass_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsGaryJBass-6">[6]</a></sup> and imposing an obligation on persons to respect the human rights of others,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordEncy_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordEncy-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsUnitedNations_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-twsUnitedNations-3">[3]</a></sup> and it is generally considered that they should not be taken away except as a result of <a href="/wiki/Due_process" title="Due process">due process</a> based on specific circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsUnitedNations_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-twsUnitedNations-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>The doctrine of human rights has been highly influential within <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> and global and regional institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsUnitedNations_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-twsUnitedNations-3">[3]</a></sup> Actions by <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">states</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organisations" title="Non-governmental organisations">non-governmental organisations</a> form a basis of <a href="/wiki/Public_policy" title="Public policy">public policy</a> worldwide. The idea of human rights suggests that "if the public discourse of peacetime global society can be said to have a common moral language, it is that of human rights".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeitz20091_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeitz20091-7">[7]</a></sup> The strong claims made by the doctrine of human rights continue to provoke considerable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scepticism" title="Scepticism">scepticism</a> and debates about the content, nature and justifications of human rights to this day. The precise meaning of the term <i><a href="/wiki/Rights" title="Rights">right</a></i> is controversial and is the subject of continued philosophical debate;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShaw2008265_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw2008265-8">[8]</a></sup> while there is consensus that human rights encompasses a wide variety of rights<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsBritannica_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsBritannica-5">[5]</a></sup> such as the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_a_fair_trial" title="Right to a fair trial">right to a fair trial</a>, protection against <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">enslavement</a>, prohibition of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">free speech</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsMacmillan_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-twsMacmillan-9">[9]</a></sup> or a <a href="/wiki/Right_to_education" title="Right to education">right to education</a>, there is disagreement about which of these particular rights should be included within the general framework of human rights;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordEncy_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordEncy-1">[1]</a></sup> some thinkers suggest that human rights should be a minimum requirement to avoid the worst-case abuses, while others see it as a higher standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordEncy_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordEncy-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> It has also been argued that human rights are "<a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>-given", although this notion has been criticized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many of the basic ideas that animated the <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_movement" title="Human rights movement">human rights movement</a> developed in the aftermath of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> and the events of <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsGaryJBass_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-twsGaryJBass-6">[6]</a></sup> culminating in the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> in Paris by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> in 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Ancient peoples did not have the same modern-day conception of universal human rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFreeman200215–17_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFreeman200215–17-13">[13]</a></sup> The true forerunner of human rights discourse was the concept of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_and_legal_rights" title="Natural and legal rights">natural rights</a> which appeared as part of the medieval <a href="/wiki/Natural_law" title="Natural law">natural law</a> tradition that became prominent during the European <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> with such philosophers as <a href="/wiki/John_Locke" title="John Locke">John Locke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Hutcheson_(philosopher)" title="Francis Hutcheson (philosopher)">Francis Hutcheson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Burlamaqui" title="Jean-Jacques Burlamaqui">Jean-Jacques Burlamaqui</a> and which featured prominently in the political discourse of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsGaryJBass_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-twsGaryJBass-6">[6]</a></sup> From this foundation, the modern human rights arguments emerged over the latter half of the 20th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoyn20108_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoyn20108-14">[14]</a></sup> possibly as a reaction to slavery, torture, genocide and war crimes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsGaryJBass_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-twsGaryJBass-6">[6]</a></sup> as a realisation of inherent human vulnerability and as being a precondition for the possibility of a <a href="/wiki/Just_society" title="Just society">just society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsBritannica_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-twsBritannica-5">[5]</a></sup> Human rights advocacy has continued into the early 21st century, centred around achieving greater economic and political freedom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twsBritannica_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-twsBritannica-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_human_rights" title="History of human rights">History of human rights</a></div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}html.client-js body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png"
